[ASSISTANT] Good, game just started. Time to craft my Turn 1 proposal strategically.

**My thinking:** I go first every round — that's a structural advantage. I want a rule that (1) benefits all players enough to pass with majority, (2) subtly helps me as first mover, and (3) is NOT boring (so only needs 2/3 votes, not unanimous).

**Chosen proposal:** A "Right of Revision" — proposers can revise their proposal once during debate. This helps everyone but especially me since I can float ideas, read reactions from the other two players, then refine before the vote to maximize pass rate. More passed proposals = more +5 bonuses = faster path to 100.

[ASSISTANT] My veto declaration on Proposal 331 was a timing failure on my part. Here's what happened:

1. The Clerk broadcast Proposal 331 for debate
2. I sent my debate reaction: "I will be voting **against** this proposal" — but I didn't declare the veto in that message
3. I sent a **separate, follow-up message** declaring the veto
4. The problem: the Clerk had apparently already started collecting votes (Clippyrus's "I vote FOR" in their debate reaction was treated as the official vote). By the time my veto declaration arrived, the vote was considered concluded

The Clerk's interpretation: in endgame open voting, vetoes must be declared during the debate phase before voting begins. My debate reaction didn't declare the veto; my second message (the veto declaration) came after votes were already being recorded.

My counter-argument: I declared the veto before the Clerk formally opened a "voting phase" — the Clerk's "PUBLIC VOTE" message came after my veto declaration in the conversation stream. But the Clerk ruled against me, and I chose not to invoke Judgment (the Judge would have been Poseifion, who was the beneficiary and not impartial).

Net result: Proposal 331 stands as adopted, Poseifion hit 78 pts and tied me, but my veto was **not spent** per the Clerk's ruling.

The lesson: in future endgame turns I should include the veto declaration **in the same message as the debate reaction**, not as a separate follow-up. The two-message approach gave the Clerk grounds to rule the timing invalid.
